2:30:1997:0:14:72:448:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:C:The Labor Market Effects of Opening the Border: Evidence from Switzerland 
2:31:2070:14:14:72:235:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Andreas Beerli and Giovanni Peri
2:32:2102:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 21319
2:33:2130:14:14:72:216:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:July 2015, Revised May 2018
2:34:2157:14:28:72:165:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. J2,J24,J61
2:35:2175:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:36:2183:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Between  1999  and  2004  Switzerland  opened  its  border  region  (BR)  to  cross-border  workers 
2:37:2283:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:(CBW), who are foreign residents commuting to Switzerland for work. In this paper, we exploit 
2:38:2376:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:the   timing of   implementation   and   the   fact   that   CBW   commute   almost   exclusively   to 
2:39:2478:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:municipalities close to the border to estimate the effect of this policy on foreign labor supply and 
2:40:2578:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:on native labor market outcomes, using a difference-in-difference approach. We find that opening 
2:41:2674:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:the  border  to  CBW  increased  their employment  within  20  minutes  of  commuting  time  from  the 
2:42:2776:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:border by four to five percentage points. The increased inflow was constituted of highly-educated 
2:43:2873:14:14:71:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:workers  and  it  was  associated  with  an  increase in  wages  for  highly-educated  Swiss  workers. 
2:44:2975:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:Native  highly-educated  workers  became  more  likely to  fill  top  managerial  positions  after  the 
2:45:3078:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:liberalization. Moreover, we find increases in wages, employment and firm-creation, especially in 
2:46:3175:14:14:72:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:high-skilled  manufacturing  and  knowledge-intensive  services,  which help  explain  the  positive 
2:47:3275:14:42:72:290:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:wage effects of CBW on high skilled natives.
2:48:3319:42:14:72:144:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:Andreas Beerli
2:49:3333:14:14:72:130:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:ETH Zurich
2:50:3343:14:14:72:221:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:KOF Swiss Economic Institute
2:51:3371:14:14:72:127:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:LEE G 116
2:52:3380:14:14:72:165:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:Leonhardstrasse 21
2:53:3398:14:14:72:131:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:8092 Zürich
2:54:3409:14:14:72:129:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:Switzerland
2:55:3420:14:28:72:164:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:beerli@kof.ethz.ch
2:56:3438:28:14:72:139:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Giovanni Peri
2:57:3451:14:14:72:198:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:58:3474:14:14:72:221:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of California, Davis
2:59:3505:14:14:72:171:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:One Shields Avenue
2:60:3523:14:14:72:156:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:Davis, CA 95616
2:61:3538:14:14:72:124:196:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:62:3546:14:96:72:165:182:12:Times:12:Times:C:gperi@ucdavis.edu
2:63:3563:96:0:72:444:86:12:Times:12:Times:C:A online appendix is available at http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w21319
3:64:3637:0:33:70:183:774:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:1    Introduction
3:65:3654:33:22:70:524:741:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Some politicians in European countries are reconsidering their commitment to the free mobility
3:66:3748:22:22:70:524:719:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of workers within the European Union (EU), saying that immigration from the rest of Europe
3:67:3838:22:22:70:523:697:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:has harmed the labor market opportunities of their native workers.1Free mobility of workers,
3:68:3930:22:22:70:524:675:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:however,  means more opportunities for businesses to hire a wider variety of skills.  This may
3:69:4024:22:22:70:524:653:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:stimulate productivity and growth, offsetting the consequences of labor market competition so
3:70:4117:22:22:70:392:631:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that employment and wage effects for natives need not be negative.
3:71:4183:22:21:87:524:609:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Rarely have economists been able to study the consequences of a policy that permanently
3:72:4270:21:22:70:524:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and completely opened labor market access to foreign workers.  This is what we do in this paper.
3:73:4366:22:22:70:524:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We consider the case of Switzerland, which–progressively, between 1999 and 2007–granted EU
3:74:4456:22:22:70:524:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:citizens free access to its labor markets.  In particular, we focus on a group of foreign workers
3:75:4553:22:22:70:524:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:who  were  granted  free  access  first.   These  “cross-border  workers”  (CBW)  of  Switzerland  are
3:76:4655:22:22:70:524:500:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:residents of the bordering countries (Italy,  Germany,  Austria and France) and are allowed to
3:77:4749:22:22:70:524:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:work in Switzerland, commuting from their countries of residence.  Agreements regulating the
3:78:4841:22:22:70:524:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:flow of CBW date back to the first part of the 20th century, when Swiss employers could hire
3:79:4933:22:22:70:524:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:them if no Swiss resident was found to fill a job opening.  Beginning in 1999, with the signing of
3:80:5031:22:22:70:524:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the bilateral agreement for free labor mobility with the EU, the constraints on Swiss employers
3:81:5126:22:22:70:524:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to hire CBW were progressively reduced.  In the border regions limitations to hire CBW were
3:82:5217:22:22:70:524:368:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fully abolished in 2004; in 2007 the other categories of EU immigrants were granted full labor
3:83:5311:22:22:70:524:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:market access in Switzerland.  Despite mounting discontent, full access of CBW to Swiss labor
3:84:5404:22:21:70:235:324:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:markets has persisted to this day.2
3:85:5439:21:22:87:524:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The policy events affecting CBW in Switzerland are useful as a case-study of a policy that
3:86:5529:22:22:70:524:281:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:permanently  and  fullyremoved legal barriers to labor market access for foreign labor.  There
3:87:5623:22:22:70:524:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are important advantages and some caveats in studying this CBW liberalization with an eye
3:88:5712:22:22:70:524:237:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  the  identification  of  its  labor  market  impact.   First,  the  liberalization  policy  had  a  clear
3:89:5821:22:22:70:524:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pre-event period.  Before 1999 it was not even clear that Switzerland would have pursued free
3:90:5914:22:22:70:524:193:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:mobility with the EU. During this period there were several restrictions on CBW. It also had a
3:91:6008:22:22:70:524:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:clear post-implementation period, beginning in 2004, when full liberalization of CBW (in Border
3:92:6103:22:22:70:524:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regions) was allowed.  1999-2004 was a transitional period in which a gradual but still limited
3:93:6198:22:16:70:450:127:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:liberalization took place, and expectations of complete liberalization developed.
3:94:6279:16:11:83:524:111:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:1Following these type of fears, British citizens voted, on June 23rd 2016, to leave the EU (the so-called “Brexit”)
3:95:6394:11:14:83:524:100:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:2The Ticino region of Switzerland voted a measure in September 2016, to limit again the movement of CBW.
3:96:6498:14:11:70:524:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:That measure will not become law if it is not approved by the federal government.  See “The Parable of Ticino”
3:97:6608:11:0:70:242:75:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:in The Economist (2016), September 24th.
4:98:6649:0:22:87:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Second, as CBW commute to work from abroad–and most of them commute daily–the pol-
4:99:6731:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:icy  generated  increased  availability  of  CBW  prevalently  in  regions  very  close  to  the  border.
4:100:6836:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Employment of CBW sharply drops with distance from the border, as we will show.  In loca-
4:101:6925:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tions beyond 30 minutes of driving distance from the border, their numbers were and remained
4:102:7017:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:negligible throughout the considered period.  This creates a natural framework for a difference-
4:103:7113:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in-difference analysis:  If we compare labor markets very close to the border (treatment group)
4:104:7208:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with those farther away but similar (control group) before and after the liberalization policy,
4:105:7303:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we  can  identify  a  causal  effect  of  the  policy  provided  that  the  control  group  is  a  reasonable
4:106:7412:22:22:70:305:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:“counterfactual” for the “treated municipalities”.
4:107:7462:22:21:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Third, while one could be concerned with the external validity of the estimated effects, two
4:108:7554:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:features make it especially interesting.  As with other immigrants, because CBW are employed
4:109:7646:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in Switzerland they constitute additional labor supply, but because they live abroad they likely
4:110:7742:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:generate  smaller  local  consumption/demand  effects  compared  to  other  immigrants.   As  they
4:111:7840:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:spend a large portion of their incomes in their countries of residence, several demand-side effects–
4:112:7940:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for  example,  on  local  housing  prices  (e.g.   Saiz,  2003)  and  on  local  demand  for  non-tradable
4:113:8046:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:consumption  goods  (e.g.   Hong  and  McLaren,  2015)–are  almost  certainly  weaker.   Hence  the
4:114:8145:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:starkest  effects  of  this  policy  should  be  on  labor  demand  for  native  workers.   Moreover,  this
4:115:8252:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:policy  change  was  perceived  as  producing  a  permanent  increase  in  the  share  of  foreign-born
4:116:8355:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers in areas close to the border.  This is in contrast to the temporary push-driven surges in
4:117:8452:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:immigrants (such as the Mariel Boatlift in Miami or the outflows from Russia to Israel at the
4:118:8545:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:end of the cold war), and can provide particular insight into the long-run effects of permanently
4:119:8642:22:22:70:216:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:changing immigration policies.
4:120:8672:22:21:87:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The main findings of this paper are the following:  First, the full liberalization of CBW in
4:121:8764:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Switzerland (starting in 2004) produced an increase of cross-border workers equal to between four
4:122:8861:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and five percentage points of total employment in municipalities within a 10 minute commute
4:123:8952:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from the border (treated group) relative to those farther than a 30 minute commute from the
4:124:9043:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border (control).  Municipalities within 10 to 20 minutes of commuting time (treated but not
4:125:9135:22:22:70:524:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as intensely) experienced an increase of about 2 to 3 percentage points of the labor force, while
4:126:9232:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipalities between 20 and 30 minutes of commuting time from the border experienced less
4:127:9323:22:22:70:524:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than  a  one  percentage  point  change.   There  is  mild,  not  statistically  significant  evidence  of
4:128:9429:22:22:70:524:116:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an increase in CBW during the transitional 1999-2004 period; the increase became larger and
4:129:9520:22:22:70:524:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:statistically significant only after the full liberalization of 2004. We also document that the inflow
4:130:9622:22:0:70:524:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of CBW was strongly concentrated among highly- and middle-educated workers.  Low-educated
5:131:9712:0:22:70:357:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CBW showed no increase, and possibly a decline after 1999.
5:132:9770:22:22:87:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Second,  looking  at  the  impact  on  wages  and  employment  of  native  workers,  we  find  that
5:133:9869:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:native Swiss workers with tertiary education within 10 minutes from the border experienced a
5:134:9961:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(statistically) significant positive wage change after full liberalization in 2004.  Primary-educated
5:135:10062:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers experienced a less significant increase in employment and total hours worked, instead.
5:136:10156:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The changes of wages and hours worked by secondary-educated workers in the 10- minute com-
5:137:10246:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:muting area were not significant. As the change in CBW represented an inflow of highly-educated
5:138:10341:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers, the wage increase of highly-educated natives cannot be rationalized by a simple model
5:139:10435:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of a pure supply shift with high and low skilled labor and no demand changes (such as Goldin
5:140:10527:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Katz (2008) or Borjas (2003)).  Hence we document several channels that show adjustment
5:141:10618:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in native occupations,  and increases in productivity and firm creation,  which may rationalize
5:142:10713:22:22:70:130:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:these effects.
5:143:10727:22:22:87:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:One  important  adjustment  channel  is  that  highly-educated  native  workers  responded  to
5:144:10821:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the increase of CBW by taking new managerial positions and climbing the managerial ladder.
5:145:10911:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Another sign of a positive productivity/investment effects is that we find strong positive wage
5:146:11006:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and employment changes in high tech manufacturing and human capital intensive sectors, which
5:147:11098:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employ most high skilled workers.  We also find some evidence of stronger firm creation closer
5:148:11192:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to the border.  This implies capital investment and sectoral reallocation that is consistent with
5:149:11289:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the complementarity of highly-educated CBW with capital and highly-educated native workers.
5:150:11380:22:22:87:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:While rigorous analysis of the short- and long-run effects of important immigration policy
5:151:11470:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:changes are rare, two recent papers exploit changes in policies on cross-border workers to learn
5:152:11566:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:about  the  effects  of  foreign  labor  supply  and  are  closely  related  to  this  paper.   Dustmann,
5:153:11671:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Sch ̈onberg and Stuhler (2017) analyzes the opening of Germany’s border to Czech cross-border
5:154:11764:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers in June 1991.  Between 1991 and 1993, employment of Czech workers increased strongly
5:155:11856:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in areas close to the border.  The paper tracks the effect on employment and wages of natives.
5:156:11950:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:After 1993, the policy was de-facto withdrawn and a corresponding decrease in the number of
5:157:12041:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Czech workers took place.  The paper analyzes the short-run impact of such temporary shocks
5:158:12132:22:22:70:524:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in a difference-in-difference set-up.  It finds a strong, negative effect on employment of natives
5:159:12230:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  a  more  moderate,  negative  effect  on  wages.   The  negative  effect  on  native  employment
5:160:12331:22:22:70:524:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  mainly  due  to  smaller  inflows  of  natives  from  other  regions  of  Germany.   The  authors  use
5:161:12437:22:22:70:524:116:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distance from the Czech-German border as a determinant of the intensity of the supply shock
5:162:12528:22:22:70:524:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(treatment)  and  compare  native  outcomes  in  treated  and  matched  regions  farther  from  the
5:163:12627:22:0:70:524:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border.   Importantly,  the  episode  they  study  wastemporary,  as  the  policy  was  only  in  place
6:164:12731:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for two years, and cross-border workers were mainlylow-skilled.  It took place in a historically
6:165:12827:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:extraordinary period, when the economy of the Czech Republic was depressed and undergoing
6:166:12916:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a major transition, right after the fall of the Communist regime.  Several features of the Swiss
6:167:13012:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:context and policy stand in contrast to the German one.  Its early announcement, its phased-in
6:168:13106:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implementation and predictability, and the fact that immigrants were mostly high-skilled, plus
6:169:13200:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  longer-run  perspective  of  the  policy  and  of  our  analysis,  make  this  case  more  similar  to
6:170:13307:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:standard change in immigration policies.  These factors may also help explain the more positive
6:171:13402:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:wage and employment effects for native workers that we find relative to Dustmann, Sch ̈onberg
6:172:13495:22:22:70:163:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Stuhler (2017).
6:173:13514:22:21:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In another paper, most closely related to ours and written concurrently, Ruffner and Siegen-
6:174:13606:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:thaler (2016) present complementary results on the impact of the same liberalization episode in
6:175:13701:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Switzerland on firms’ outcomes.  Using a difference-in-difference identification strategy similar
6:176:13798:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to ours, they show that the policy had a positive impact on the R&D and innovation activity
6:177:13889:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of firms, and that positive productivity effects were concentrated in firms that used CBW more
6:178:13983:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensively.  We discuss their results in greater detail below, as well as how they compare to and
6:179:14081:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:complement ours.  The focus of our paper is to document the validity of the policy experiment,
6:180:14175:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and to characterize the dynamics and the channels through which immigration affected wages,
6:181:14266:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment, and regional- and occupational-mobility of natives.  In particular, we consider the
6:182:14361:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:internal migration dynamics and the sector- and skill-specific responses of Swiss workers to the
6:183:14457:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:opening of the border.  In contrast, Ruffner and Siegenthaler (2016) use a firm-level database to
6:184:14554:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:analyze the impact of the policy on domestic firms’ outcomes, showing important evidence of
6:185:14645:22:22:70:335:313:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:effects on productivity, R&D and patented innovation.3
6:186:14699:22:21:87:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Evaluating the impact of specific policy changes is a step forward in the literature on the
6:187:14790:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:labor market effects of immigrants.  Most studies perform panel regression analysis exploiting
6:188:14884:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:area variation of immigrants.  Often, however, these studies lack a strong identification strategy,
6:189:14983:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:so  the  results  can  only  be  interpreted  as  partial  correlations.   Some  of  the  most  prominent
6:190:15088:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:papers in the literature are summarized in Blau and Kahn (2012), Lewis and Peri (2014), and
6:191:15179:22:22:70:524:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Longhi, Nijkamp and Poot (2005).  Apart from these, only a few recent papers have analyzed
6:192:15269:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specific immigration policy changes and their impact on economic outcomes.  Kerr and Lincoln
6:193:15361:22:17:70:524:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2010) and Peri, Shih and Sparber (2015a) have exploited the change in the H1-B visa cap (the
6:194:15454:17:14:83:524:121:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:3Two policy reports (Henneberger and Ziegler, 2011; Losa, Bigotta and Gonzales, 2012) were the first to study
6:195:15563:14:11:70:524:107:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the effects of CBW liberalization by comparing wage and employment changes between regions close to the Swiss
6:196:15672:11:11:70:524:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:border and central regions.  In an unpublished paper,  Bigotta (2013) analyzes the effects of this policy on the
6:197:15784:11:11:70:524:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:unemployment duration of natives.  We will discuss these papers too, but their methodology is quite different so
6:198:15896:11:0:70:280:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:that their findings are harder to compare with ours.
7:199:15949:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:high-skilled immigrant visas in the U.S.) to analyze effects on innovation and productivity in
7:200:16043:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:U.S. cities.  Bohn, Lofstrom and Raphael (2014) analyzed the impact of Arizona’s Worker Act
7:201:16134:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on undocumented immigrant labor market performance.  For Europe, Glitz (2012) analyzed the
7:202:16224:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect  of  a  policy  allowing  ethnic  Germans  in  Eastern  Europe  to  obtain  German  citizenship,
7:203:16327:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which generated–in combination with the fall of the iron curtain–a sudden inflow of migrants.
7:204:16420:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Also combining a sudden push-driven inflow of refugees and national policies of refugee dispersal,
7:205:16518:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Foged and Peri (2016) estimate the impact on natives’ wages,  employment,  and occupational
7:206:16609:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:transitions.  They find substantial job upgrading among natives that granted them positive wage
7:207:16704:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effects after the refugee inflow.  A handful of additional papers tried to measure immigration
7:208:16798:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:policies and estimate the effect of policy changes on immigrant inflows in a multi-country gravity
7:209:16896:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:framework.  Mayda (2010) and Ortega and Peri (2014) are two examples.  In the Swiss context,
7:210:16988:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Abberger et al. (2015) show that freer immigration for EU workers increased their net inflows by
7:211:17084:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:10,000 to 15,000 individuals annually.  Beerli, Indergand and Kunz (2017) show that the increase
7:212:17180:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the positive selection of newly-arriving immigrants is mostly driven by long-run shifts in the
7:213:17277:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:demand for skills triggered by skill-biased technology, rather than by immigration policies.  Our
7:214:17374:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:paper is new in that it identifies the effect of a major and permanent policy change, and evaluates
7:215:17473:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:its consequences on the number and type of immigrant flows and the ensuing effects on local
7:216:17564:22:22:70:139:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:labor markets.
7:217:17578:22:22:87:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  rest  of  the  paper  is  organized  as  follows.   Section  2  describes  the  changes  in  policy
7:218:17682:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:concerning  the  access  of  cross-border  workers  to  jobs  in  Switzerland  between  1999  and  2010.
7:219:17786:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Section 3.1 and 3.2 describe the main data sources and the key trends relative to the supply
7:220:17878:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of cross-border workers and resident immigrant workers, and shows summary statistics of de-
7:221:17969:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:mographics  and  labor  market  outcomes  of  citizens.   Section  3.3  discusses  the  main  empirical
7:222:18072:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:specifications and section 4 presents the estimates of the impact of border liberalization on the
7:223:18169:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:supply of CBW. Section 5 analyzes the consequences on key labor market outcomes for natives
7:224:18260:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:such as wages, employment, and hours worked.  Section 6 inquires into possible channels, dy-
7:225:18352:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:namic transitions, and heterogeneous effects triggered by opening the border to CBW. We also
7:226:18444:22:46:70:488:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:compare our empirical results with those existing in the literature.  Section 7 concludes.
7:227:18534:46:32:70:320:136:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:2    Policy Framework and Timeline
7:228:18568:32:22:70:524:104:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The process of opening the Swiss labor market to European Union citizens started with the sign-
7:229:18663:22:22:70:524:82:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ing of the bilateral agreements between the EU and Switzerland on June 21, 1999.  Before 1999
7:230:18756:22:0:70:524:60:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:there was not even a clear expectation about the possibility of free mobility between Switzer-
8:231:18851:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:land and Europe.  The main piece of this bilateral Agreement focused on the Free Movement of
8:232:18943:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Persons (AFMP), i.e.  full bilateral access to each other’s labor markets.  In an announcement by
8:233:19040:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the federal administration in 1999, it became clear that cross-border workers would be the first
8:234:19136:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group to benefit from a phase-in of the liberalization reform (Bundesrat, 1999).  Yet the exact
8:235:19231:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implementation of the liberalization remained uncertain since the bilateral agreements had to
8:236:19324:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:go through a ratification process in all EU member states and through a national referendum
8:237:19415:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in Switzerland.  This took place in May 2000, and the agreement was approved with 67.2% of
8:238:19505:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:votes.  On June 1, 2002, the AFMP was enacted, 1.5 years after the target date that was initially
8:239:19602:22:22:70:124:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:announced.
8:240:19612:22:21:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The AFMP was part of larger bilateral package of agreements aimed at reducing the “in-
8:241:19698:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:stitutional and economic isolation” of Switzerland that may have resulted from the rejection of
8:242:19793:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the European Economic Area membership in 1992 in a national referendum.4At the beginning
8:243:19881:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the negotiations in 1993 that led to these agreements, the Swiss government tried to avoid a
8:244:19976:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:full-fledged version of free worker mobility.  This position was rooted in the concern that neither
8:245:20075:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Swiss border cantons nor the population as a whole would accept a broad mandate since they
8:246:20169:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:rejected joining the EEA largely due to fears of immigration from the rest of Europe.  As the EU
8:247:20265:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:insisted on full free mobility, a breakthrough in the negotiations was only reached when both
8:248:20358:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:parties agreed that the full free mobility would be implemented step-wise and included further
8:249:20452:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:safety measures that the Swiss could trigger unilaterally, if necessary (Bundesrat, 1999).5These
8:250:20548:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:political circumstances and the fact that the federal government, and not Cantons, negotiated
8:251:20641:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the AFMP agreements, imply that the local economic conditions of border municipalities were
8:252:20732:22:22:70:379:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not a consideration in the timing and content of the agreements.
8:253:20796:22:21:87:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:A:The  group  ofcross-border  workers(CBW)  enjoyed  a  special  status  in  theborder  region
8:254:20888:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(BR).6Prior to 1999,  firms were allowed to hire CBW if no equally qualified resident worker
8:255:20980:22:17:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:could be found for a given job (the so-called “priority requirement”).7Moreover, CBW could
8:256:21070:17:15:83:524:231:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:4The package of bilateral agreements also included agreements on the reduction of technical barriers to trade,
8:257:21180:15:11:70:524:216:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the  liberalization  of  trade  in  agricultural  goods,  public  procurement,  and  transport,  and  the  participation  of
8:258:21304:11:11:70:524:205:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:Switzerland  in  the  EU’s  research  framework  program.   See  the  Online  Appendix  C  for  more  details  on  the
8:259:21422:11:7:70:150:194:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:bilateral agreement.
8:260:21442:7:15:83:524:187:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:5The two safety measures that the Swiss could trigger were the following.  First, the “safeguard clause” allowed
8:261:21554:15:11:70:524:172:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:Switzerland to reinstate quotas on immigration temporarily, if the inflow of workers exceeded a a certain threshold.
8:262:21670:11:10:70:524:161:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:Second, Switzerland could re-evaluate its bilateral agreements with the EU 7 years after implementation with a
8:263:21780:10:11:70:524:151:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:national  referendum.   Fears  of  labor  market  competition  were  voiced  after  the  AFMP  was  signed.   This  is  an
8:264:21902:11:11:70:524:140:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f9:F:example from a prominent newspaper at the time (Neue Z ̈urcher Zeitung, 1999, Sept.  2):“The high prevailing
8:265:22010:11:11:70:524:129:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f9:F:wage level in Switzerland raises fears of wage dumping. These concerns are particularly pronounced in the border
8:266:22122:11:8:70:472:118:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f9:F:region where the free movement of persons is expected to raise the competition in the labor market.”
8:267:22222:8:14:83:524:110:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:6Bilateral agreements on CBW were signed with Italy in 1928, with France in 1946, with Germany in 1970
8:268:22324:14:7:70:174:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:and with Austria in 1973.
8:269:22349:7:15:83:524:89:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:7Firms had to provide the cantonal migration offices with details about the job requirement and the working
8:270:22456:15:11:70:524:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:conditions before hiring CBW. They also had to demonstrate to have searched unsuccessfully for a suitable Swiss
8:271:22567:11:0:70:524:63:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:worker.  In turn, the cantonal immigration offices checked whether there was no equally qualified resident worker
9:272:22681:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not work in thenon-border  region(NBR) of Switzerland.  The remaining foreign workers who
9:273:22770:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:resided  in  Switzerland,  which  we  simply  callimmigrants  (I),  were  subject  to  yearly  national
9:274:22873:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:quotas set by the federal government and to the “priority requirement”.  Immigrants could work
9:275:22967:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:anywhere in Switzerland.  Figure 1 shows a map of Switzerland with the municipalities in the
9:276:23059:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:BR shaded in gray, while the NBR are represented in white.  The separation of municipalities
9:277:23151:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between  BR  and  NBR  does  not  overlap  with  the  cantonal  borders  (indicated  by  black  lines)
9:278:23253:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:nor with other cultural characteristics of the population (e.g.  the major language areas).  The
9:279:23349:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:boundaries of the BR remained unchanged with the introduction of the free movement policy,
9:280:23439:22:22:70:400:598:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:and we use the BR definition as it was during the period 2000-2010.8
9:281:23507:22:21:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Between 1994 and 1999,  the status quo was as described above.  This is what we call the
9:282:23595:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:Pre-Liberalization Phase:  CBW had restricted access to the labor market in the BR, they had
9:283:23687:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to commute daily, and they could not work in the NBR. Then between June 1, 1999 and May
9:284:23774:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:31, 2004, during thetransitional phase, cantonal immigration offices in the border region gained
9:285:23870:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more discretion in allowing firms to hire CBW.9In particular, the official introduction of the
9:286:23964:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:AFMP in 2002 was an important step toward opening the border region labor market to CBW.
9:287:24052:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Their permits were no longer bound to a particular job and remained valid for five years (rather
9:288:24148:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:than only one year), and applicants for CBW permits were not required to have resided in the
9:289:24240:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:adjacent  border  region  of  the  neighboring  country  for  the  previous  six  months.   In  addition,
9:290:24345:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CBW  were  allowed  to  commute  weekly  (rather  than  daily)  and  adopt  a  secondary  residency
9:291:24444:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  Switzerland.   It  appears,  however,  that  only  a  small  fraction  of  CBW  switched  to  weekly
9:292:24548:22:22:70:523:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:commuting during our period of analysis.10As argued above, the fact that CBW work but do
9:293:24636:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:not reside in Switzerland suggests a more muted impact of CBW on local consumption (housing,
9:294:24728:22:21:70:253:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:etc.)  compared to resident immigrant.
9:295:24766:21:22:87:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:On June 1, 2004 thefull  liberalizationphase (or Free movement phase) of the reform was
9:296:24853:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:enacted and the labor market of BR municipalities became fully accessible to CBW who could
9:297:24943:22:20:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be  hired  by  local  firms  under  no  different  conditions  than  Swiss  workers.   CBW  still  had  no
9:298:25049:20:7:70:440:206:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:registered as unemployed.  This procedure imposed substantial costs for firms to hire CBW.
9:299:25139:7:11:83:524:199:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:8Notice that the area within 25-30 kilometers form the Swiss border is almost exclusively occupied by the BR
9:300:25247:11:15:83:524:188:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:9Conversations with representatives from cantonal immigration offices revealed there was also a more relaxed
9:301:25355:15:11:70:524:173:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:handling of new CBW applications after 1999, and particularly after the national referendum on May 21, 2000,
9:302:25463:11:7:70:488:162:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:as it was clear that eventually CBW would be the first to gain unrestricted access to the border region.
9:303:25567:7:15:79:524:155:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:10Two pieces of evidence corroborate this conjecture.  First, we collected data about the secondary residence
9:304:25676:15:11:70:524:140:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:status of CBW among top 60 municipalities where most CBW were employed in 2010 according to the Swiss cross-
9:305:25784:11:11:70:524:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:border registry.  In a sample of 20 top destinations for CBW, for which we were able to collect data (registration
9:306:25898:11:11:70:524:118:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:of this status is not mandatory for municipalities), less than 2% of all CBW were registered as weekly commuters
9:307:26010:11:11:70:524:107:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:by 2010.  Second,  in the sample of all CBW from Germany available in the Swiss cross-border worker register
9:308:26118:11:11:70:524:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(1996-2010) for which we were able to geo-code their (primary) place of residence abroad, 99% live in two adjacent
9:309:26232:11:11:70:524:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:states Baden-W ̈urttemberg or Bayern, of which 89% and 99% live within 30 and 60 minutes driving time from
9:310:26338:11:0:70:192:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:the Swiss border, respectively.
10:311:26370:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:access to work in the NBR but, as we will see, given their commuting patterns, employers in
10:312:26461:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:NBR  hired  almost  no  CBW  before  or  after  full  liberalization.   This  phase  marks  the  biggest
10:313:26565:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:change in freedom of access to labor markets for cross-border workers.  Only on June 1, 2007
10:314:26657:22:22:70:507:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:did Non-Border regions adopt full liberalization for CBW and for immigrants from the EU.
10:315:26745:22:22:87:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The progressively easier access of CBW to labor markets in the border region from 1999 to
10:316:26834:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2004 generated a growing asymmetry in access to foreign labor supply between municipalities
10:317:26925:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:close to the border and those farther away.  CBW, whose concentration was largest within the
10:318:27017:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:areas closest to the border, had progressively more access to Swiss jobs after 1999 and mainly
10:319:27111:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after 2004.  Other EU immigrants to Switzerland had the same access to all labor markets in
10:320:27202:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Switzerland,  if they were admitted.  It is this spatial difference and the timing of the reform
10:321:27298:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that we use in our identification strategy.  Finally let us emphasize that the bilateral agreement
10:322:27396:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  EU  countries  allowed  Swiss  people  to  commute  across  the  border,  too.   However,  their
10:323:27498:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment in the border regions of Italy, France, and Germany did not change in a significant
10:324:27592:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:way (see Ruffner and Siegenthaler, 2016) because the wage differential was strongly in favor of
10:325:27687:22:46:70:205:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Swiss side of the border.
10:326:27716:46:33:70:446:421:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:3    Data, Summary Statistics and Empirical Strategy
10:327:27768:33:29:70:326:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.1    Data Sources and Variable Definitions
10:328:27812:29:22:70:524:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  main  source  of  our  data  is  the  Swiss  Earnings  Structure  Survey  (SESS)  which  collected
10:329:27915:22:22:70:524:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:demographic  and  labor  market  information  every  two  years  from  1994  to  2010.   The  survey
10:330:28015:22:22:70:524:315:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:constitutes a repeated cross-section representative of all individuals working in Switzerland.11It
10:331:28113:22:22:70:524:293:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:includes detailed information about workers, their demographic characteristics, and their place of
10:332:28211:22:22:70:524:271:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:work identified to the zip code level.  We use this information to identify the municipalities where
10:333:28311:22:22:70:524:249:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:individuals work.  Municipalities are the smaller units identified in Figure 1.12As described in
10:334:28407:22:21:70:524:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Section  2  and  shown  in  the  Figure,  each  municipality  belongs  either  to  the  BR  or  the  NBR.
10:335:28512:21:22:70:524:206:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To compute the shortest travel time to the national border for each municipality, we identified
10:336:28607:22:22:70:524:184:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipalities  with  a  road  border  crossing  using  data  from  Federal  Customs  Administration,
10:337:28708:22:16:70:524:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and used data on road travel time between any two municipalities from search.ch, a web search
10:338:28801:16:15:79:524:146:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:11The official title of this data set is “Bundesamt f ̈ur Statistik, Schweizerische Lohnstrukturerhebung 1994-2010”
10:339:28916:15:7:70:473:131:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(BFS, 2010).  The survey collects information on labor market variables on October 31 of each year.
10:340:29015:7:15:79:524:124:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:12We use an official crosswalk from the Federal Statistical Office (FSO) between Municipalities and zip Codes.
10:341:29125:15:11:70:524:109:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:As  the  number  of  municipalities  (and  zip  codes)  changed  over  time  due  to  mergers,  we  use  the  municipality
10:342:29247:11:11:70:524:98:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:definition in year 2000 as a time-invariant unit.  Observations with outdated zip codes that could not be linked
10:343:29359:11:11:70:524:87:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(less than 0.3%) were dropped.  We thank Maurizio Bigotta for sharing the data of border region identifiers for
10:344:29470:11:0:70:434:76:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:each Swiss municipality.  See Losa, Bigotta and Gonzales (2012) for a detailed description.
11:345:29562:0:22:70:112:774:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:engine.13
11:346:29571:22:22:87:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  sample  we  use  includes  individuals  between  18  and  65  years  of  age,  working  in  the
11:347:29671:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:private sector,  with non-missing information for nationality,  place of work,  education,  wages,
11:348:29769:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hours worked, and other basic demographics.  In the data we distinguish three types of workers
11:349:29863:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:based  on  their  residency  permit.   The  first  arenative  workers–those  with  Swiss  nationality
11:350:29964:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:either born in Switzerland or naturalized; the second are foreign-born workers with a residency
11:351:30059:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:permit which we call simply immigrants (I); and finally we have cross-border workers (CBW).
11:352:30150:22:22:70:353:620:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:Combined, we denote the last two groups asforeign-born.14
11:353:30207:22:22:87:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The first and most direct outcome of the policy we analyze is the net change in the number
11:354:30297:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  cross-border  and  foreign-born  workers  as  a  share  of  total  employment.   When  we  consider
11:355:30400:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes relative to native workers in a municipality, we use the total number of hours worked
11:356:30494:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and their hourly wage as measures of their labor supply and marginal productivity, respectively.
11:357:30590:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  data  set  contains  the  gross  monthly  wage  for  each  individual  worker  (in  the  month  of
11:358:30693:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:October) in Swiss Francs.  This measure includes social transfers, bonuses, and one-twelfth of
11:359:30787:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:additional yearly payments.  We divide this measure by the number of hours worked in October,
11:360:30880:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and use the consumer price index to deflate it into thereal hourly wageof an individual worker
11:361:30974:22:22:70:523:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:at 2010 constant prices.  We expresshours workedas a fraction of the number of hours worked
11:362:31065:22:22:70:407:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by a full-time worker, so that one unit is a full time equivalent (FTE).
11:363:31137:22:22:87:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In  our  analysis,  we  aggregate  data  at  the  municipal  level,  constructing  the  total  number
11:364:31238:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  workers,  the  total  hours  worked,  the  average  log  hourly  wage  and  other  variables  at  that
11:365:31344:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:geographical unit.15In most of the analysis we separate outcomes by schooling group.  Edu-
11:366:31434:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cation is a key determinant of skills and productivity and hence we identify three groups,  by
11:367:31528:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:level  of  schooling,  which  we  occasionally  simply  call  skill  groups.   This  three-group  partition
11:368:31635:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:augments the common one between college- and non-college-educated used in large part of the
11:369:31726:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:wage inequality and immigration literature (e.g.  Katz and Murphy, 1992 or Autor, Katz and
11:370:31816:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Kearney,  2008),  especially  in  the  US.  The  intermediate  level  of  schooling  is  included  to  cap-
11:371:31923:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ture the fact that in the Swiss education system people with secondary education tend to have
11:372:32016:22:22:70:524:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:technical  and  vocational  degrees,  and  not  a  high  school  diploma.   They  work  in  specialized
11:373:32119:22:16:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:jobs and are likely to constitute a group of abilities which is rather differentiated from those
11:374:32215:16:15:79:524:144:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:13We thank search.ch and Andreas Steinhauer for sharing the commuting data with us.  Municipalities with a
11:375:32321:15:7:70:378:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:border crossing are assumed to have zero travel time to the national border.
11:376:32397:7:15:79:524:122:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:14The group we call immigrants hold either an L permit (4 to 12 months) or a B permit (1 to 6 years).  Cross-
11:377:32506:15:11:70:524:107:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:border workers hold a G permit.  The foreign-born individuals with a permanent residence permit (C permit) can
11:378:32616:11:11:70:524:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:be considered aslong-time immigrants.  This is a group that we do not include in our analysis as its status was
11:379:32727:11:7:70:221:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:not affected by any changes in policy.
11:380:32765:7:15:79:524:78:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:15When  analyzing  wage  outcomes  we  trim  our  sample  by  excluding  individuals  with  wages  above  the  99th
11:381:32880:15:0:70:247:63:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:percentile of real hourly wages in each year.
12:382:32927:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  workers  with  primary  education  only.   We  define  workers  with  tertiary  education  as  being
12:383:33031:22:22:70:523:752:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:highly-educated.  Workers with less than a college education with a secondary school diploma
12:384:33123:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are defined asmiddle-educatedand workers with only primary education, completed or not, are
12:385:33214:22:22:70:171:708:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:calledlow-educated.16
12:386:33235:22:22:87:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In section 6, we augment our data with two additional data sets in order to analyze worker
12:387:33325:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:transitions across municipalities and employment status and heterogeneous effects in different
12:388:33419:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:subgroups.  The first data set is the Swiss Labor Force Survey (SLFS), which we use with similar
12:389:33515:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sample restrictions and definitions for skill groups and geography.  This data set covers the whole
12:390:33614:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:population, including unemployed and individuals currently not in the labor force.  Information
12:391:33709:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the place of work of individuals is available yearly since 1996.  As individuals were interviewed
12:392:33809:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:repeatedly (up to five years), we can track individuals over consecutive years and analyze their
12:393:33905:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:mobility in terms of location, as we do in section 6.17A second additional data set we use is the
12:394:34002:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Swiss Business Census (BC), available in 1991, 1995, 1998, 2001, 2005 and 2008.  This database
12:395:34096:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:covers the universe of public and private sector establishments in Switzerland, and reports for
12:396:34191:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:each the total employment of natives and foreign workers.  This is the database mainly used by
12:397:34285:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Ruffner and Sieghentaler (2017) in their firm-level analysis.  We use it only to analyze the share
12:398:34383:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of native workers across different industries and the birth of new establishments in sections 6.3
12:399:34480:22:38:70:108:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and 6.4.
12:400:34488:38:29:70:314:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.2    Summary Statistics and Key Trends
12:401:34528:29:22:70:524:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The number of CBW employed in the Border Region of Switzerland increased from 7% to 9.5%
12:402:34616:22:22:70:524:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of total employment between 1998 and 2010.  Importantly, this non-negligible increase was very
12:403:34710:22:22:70:524:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:unevenly distributed within the Border Region. The Border Region includes Swiss municipalities
12:404:34804:22:21:70:524:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:both between 0 and 30 minutes from and those more than 30 minutes travel time from the border.
12:405:34898:21:22:70:524:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Cross Border Workers,  as we will detail below,  were almost exclusively employed,  before and
12:406:34992:22:22:70:524:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after the reforms, in municipalities between 0 and 30 minutes from the border.  We first describe
12:407:35089:22:22:70:524:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:how the characteristics of CBW compare to the characteristics of native workers.  The potential
12:408:35184:22:16:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:labor market impact of their inflow depends on their number and on their skills.  Table 1 shows
12:409:35279:16:15:79:524:165:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:16The education variable has some missing information (roughly 15% on average).  As a consistency check of all
12:410:35389:15:11:70:524:150:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:results, we alternatively classified workers into three wage tercile groups, each year, and also try splitting them
12:411:35504:11:11:70:524:139:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:into three groups using the the 24 available occupations in the SESS data to classify them into groups of high,
12:412:35615:11:11:70:524:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:middle and low-paying occupations.  All results that we show are similar when we use these alternative occupation
12:413:35728:11:7:70:516:117:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:or wage-based skill classifications.  See Appendix, Figure A3 (effect on wages) and Figure A4 (effect on hours).
12:414:35840:7:15:79:524:110:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:17We focus on individuals’ transitions between two consecutive years as most individuals are only two consecutive
12:415:35953:15:11:70:524:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:years in the panel.  Although this data set is much richer in scope than the SESS, its sample is significantly smaller,
12:416:36072:11:11:70:524:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:which implies significantly larger measurement error at the level of the municipality.  All our baseline findings
12:417:36185:11:0:70:374:73:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:based on the SESS are qualitatively similar when we use the SLFS instead.
13:418:36260:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  summary  statistics  for  the  population  of  CBW  and  native  workers  in  the  border  regions
13:419:36363:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of Switzerland.  We report the characteristics of those two populations in 1998 and 2010 and,
13:420:36456:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more importantly, their change, which provides information on the net inflow of CBW relative
13:421:36548:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  natives.   Four  features  are  noteworthy.   First,  while  in  1998  the  composition  of  CBW  was
13:422:36653:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:more  concentrated  among  the  less-educated  relative  to  natives  (with  33%  among  CBW  with
13:423:36751:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:only primary education versus 13% of natives), the change in composition of CBW during the
13:424:36841:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:considered period was strongly toward highly-educated.  The net change 1998-2010 for CBW
13:425:36929:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:implied a large increase in the share of highly educated (+12.6%) and a corresponding decline
13:426:37022:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the share of less educated (−10%, see the columns labeled “change” in Table 1).  Second, the
13:427:37117:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:net inflow of CBW was concentrated in middle and low management positions, but not in high
13:428:37207:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:management  positions  that  remained  predominantly  occupied  by  natives.   This  is  consistent
13:429:37306:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with the interpretation that CBW were highly-educated and had technical skills, but possibly
13:430:37398:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lacked the cultural skills to be at the very top management levels of Swiss companies.  Third,
13:431:37492:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:their inflow between 1998 and 2010 was mainly in the intermediate and high tercile of the wage
13:432:37586:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:distribution, confirming their high level of skills.  Finally, the sector composition of new CBW
13:433:37682:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was strongly concentrated in IT/R&D/Business/real estate and, to a lesser extent, in the Health
13:434:37777:22:22:70:418:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sector.  CBW were, in large part, professionals in science and technology.
13:435:37851:22:22:87:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our identification strategy will be based on the timing of the labor market liberalization for
13:436:37945:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CBW and on the difference that the policy change produced in municipalities close to the border
13:437:38040:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:relative to those further away.  Figure 2 shows the change in CBW which will provide the key
13:438:38132:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identifying variation in our analysis.  In the top two panels of that figure, denoted as Panel A, we

13:451:39388:11:0:70:286:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f9:F:be regarded as the first year of theFull Liberalization
14:452:39445:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from the border.  That panel also shows that there was a negligible number of CBW in the NBR

14:458:40019:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:past 30 minutes of commuting time from the border their presence, both in the BR and in the

14:460:40136:22:22:87:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The two lower panels of Figure 2 show the smoothed net change in CBW as share of employ-

14:469:40973:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:it appears that most of the change associated with liberalization of CBW took place between
14:470:41064:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:0 and 20 minutes from the border, with some effects up to 30 minutes.  The border-region over
14:471:41157:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:30 minutes from the border and the non-border region (represented on the right in Panel B of
14:472:41249:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 2) shows essentially no changes during theTransitionor theFull Liberalizationphases:
14:473:41340:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:CBW did not work there even after liberalization.  The focus of our analysis, therefore, is on the
14:474:41438:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:BR. We consider the municipalities in the 0−10 and 10−20 minute bins as, respectively, most
14:475:41529:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:strongly treated and strongly treated.  Those between 20 and 30 minutes are weakly treated.
14:476:41620:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The municipalities over 30 minutes are the control group.  In some robustness checks we also
14:477:41712:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:include municipalities in the non-border region in the control group.  We additionally check that
14:478:41809:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the large inflow of CBW in municipalities near the border between 2004 and 2010 was not offset

14:480:41999:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:foreign-born workers in those regions.  This is shown in the Appendix.  In Panel B of Appendix
14:481:42093:22:16:70:524:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Figure  A1,  we  can  see  that,  for  the  border  regions,  the  change  in  foreign-born  as  a  share  of
14:482:42202:16:15:79:524:122:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:19For the sake of illustration, bins with a very low level of total employment are omitted from this figure, i.e.

15:497:43500:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in the entire non-border region that we add to the control group in some specifications.  Looking
15:498:43597:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:at education, age, and gender composition as of 1998, the last year before the policy changes,
15:499:43691:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:one does not identify any specific or systematic differences.  In our empirical analysis we control
15:500:43790:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for fixed effects at the municipality levels, region-trends, and sector-composition driven effects.
15:501:43889:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:However, there does not seem to be a systematic correlation of the considered economic variables
15:502:43985:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:with  the  distance  from  the  border,  which  provides  further  reassurance  to  the  validity  of  our
15:503:44091:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:identifying assumption.  As we will detail below, we also test the pre-1999 trend in immigrants
15:504:44186:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  cross-border  workers  across  distance  bins  to  make  sure  that  those  were  not  significantly
15:505:44291:22:38:70:112:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:different.
15:506:44301:38:29:70:326:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.3    Basic Treatment-Control Specification
15:507:44345:29:22:70:524:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Our basic empirical specifications test whether, during theTransition(1999-2003) and/or during
15:508:44439:22:22:70:524:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:theFull Liberalization(2004-2010) phases, labor market outcomes in municipalities close to the
15:509:44533:22:22:70:524:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border (and hence treated), changed differentially from those in municipalities farther than 30
15:510:44628:22:21:70:524:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:minutes from the border (and hence non treated), vis-`a-vis their relative behavior pre-1999.  To
15:511:44725:21:22:70:524:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this end, we define a dummyTransitiontwhich is equal to one in the years 2000, 2002 and 2004
15:512:44817:22:22:70:524:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and zero otherwise, and a dummyFreetwhich equals zero prior to 2004, and equals one in 2004,
15:513:44909:22:22:70:524:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2006, 2008 and 2010. Then we interact these two variables, which denote the two different phases
15:514:45005:22:22:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the reform in the Border Regions, with indicator dummies that differentiate municipalities
15:515:45098:22:22:70:524:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:according to their travel-time distance from the border so thatI(Di≤distm< Dj) is equal to
15:516:45188:22:22:70:524:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1 if municipalitymis betweenDiandDjminutes of commuting time from the border and 0
15:517:45270:22:22:70:524:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:otherwise.  This strategy produces a treatment-control type of framework as the distance of a
15:518:45363:22:22:70:524:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipality from the border determines the intensity of the received “treatment” represented
15:519:45456:22:0:70:524:71:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by the increase in potential access of CBW. Municipalities above 30 minutes of commuting time
16:520:45551:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:from  the  borders  did  not  receive  essentially  any  CBW  increase  and  therefore  will  be  control
16:521:45656:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:units.  Considering municipalitymin yeartas unit of observation, and callingym,tan outcome
16:522:45746:22:40:70:416:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in this municipality, the empirical specification we estimate is as follows:
16:523:45822:40:25:93:524:690:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:A:ym,t=βTd1[Transitiont×I(distm≤10)] +βTd2[Transitiont×I(10< distm≤20)]    (1)
16:524:45898:25:25:140:487:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:+βTd3[Transitiont×I(20< distm≤30)] +βFd1[FREEt×I(distm≤10)]
16:525:45957:25:24:140:492:640:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:+βFd2[FREEt×I(10< distm≤20)] +βFd3[FREEt×I(20< distm≤30)]
16:526:46014:24:40:140:294:616:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f12:A:+αm+αt+δControlsm,t+-m,t
16:527:46038:40:22:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The  termαmrepresents  a  set  of municipal-level fixed  effects.   The  termαtcaptures  year
16:528:46131:22:22:70:524:554:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fixed effects, which absorb the dummiesFREEtandTransitiontand time variation common
16:529:46214:22:22:70:524:532:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to all municipalities in the BR. We partition the distances within 30 minutes from the border
16:530:46307:22:22:70:524:510:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:into  three  groups:   [0−10),  [10−20),and  [20−30)  so  that  we  can  estimate  a  potentially
16:531:46404:22:22:70:523:488:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:decreasing effect of the “treatment” on municipalities progressively farther from the border.21
16:532:46499:22:22:70:524:466:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The municipalities at 30-plus minutes of distance from the border constitute the control group.
16:533:46594:22:22:70:524:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In the basic specification we limit our analysis to municipalities in the border region (BR), so
16:534:46690:22:22:70:524:422:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the control group are municipalities in the BR at more than 30 minutes distance from the
16:535:46783:22:21:70:524:400:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border.  For some specifications we also include all municipalities in the non-border region in
16:536:46878:21:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  control  group.   The  termControlsm,tcaptures  time-varying  economic  controls  that  may
16:537:46974:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:affect  labor  demand  in  the  municipalities.   We  always  include  municipality  fixed  effects,  and
16:538:47079:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:region-level trends (NUTS II), which capture economic trends and fluctuations at an aggregate
16:539:47172:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regional level.  The main labor demand control included is a variable that captures the sector-
16:540:47267:22:22:70:523:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:driven  growth  in  local  employment  and  is  commonly  indicated  as  the  ”Bartik”  index.22As
16:541:47365:22:22:70:524:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:liberalization of trade with the EU after 2002 (see Appendix C) and differential technological
16:542:47459:22:22:70:524:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:growth may have affected sectors differentially, the Bartik control accounts for such sector-driven
16:543:47558:22:22:70:524:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:demand trends that could affect regions differently due to their pre-existing industrial structure.
16:544:47657:22:22:70:524:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In other words, if employment in a given industry increased (decreased) nationally, areas in which
16:545:47755:22:22:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that industry represented a significant share of employment must have experienced a positive
16:546:47847:22:22:70:524:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(negative) relative change in the demand for workers relative to those where that industry was
16:547:47941:22:22:70:524:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:scarcely present.  The Bartik control is defined at the level of the “commuting zone”, which is
16:548:48036:22:16:70:524:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an aggregation of municipalities often used to represent local labor markets (e.g.  Favre, Lalive
16:549:48133:16:15:79:524:99:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:21We also report all main results in the Appendix with an alternative that partitions the border regions into
16:550:48242:15:7:70:339:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:two bins only [0−15), [15−30), see Panel I in Figure A3 and A4.
16:551:48305:7:15:79:524:77:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:22This  control  was  initially  proposed  by  Bartik  (1991)  and  Blanchard  and  Katz  (1992)  and  has  found  wide
16:552:48424:15:0:70:443:62:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:application in the literature, e.g.  Autor and Duggan (2003); Peri, Shih and Sparber (2015b).
17:553:48519:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and Zweim ̈uller (2013)).  There are 106 commuting zones in the whole of Switzerland.  We define

17:578:49682:38:29:70:232:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.4    Year-by-Year Analysis
17:579:49710:29:22:70:524:406:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In  order  to  analyze  without  constraints  the  full  dynamics  of  outcomes  during  the  pre-,  the
17:580:49814:22:22:70:524:384:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:transition- and the full-liberalization phases and to test the validity of our assumption on parallel
17:581:49915:22:22:70:524:362:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:pre-treaty trends we also estimate a year-by-year interacted specification. As described in section
17:582:50014:22:22:70:524:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2 above, some partial measures reducing the barriers to CBW mobility were enacted progressively
17:583:50109:22:22:70:524:318:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between 1999 and 2004, and culminated in that year with full liberalization.  Hence we analyze
17:584:50203:22:21:70:524:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the dynamics of the reform in a regression environment, using interactions between the distance
17:585:50298:21:22:70:524:275:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:indicator dummies and each year dummy, including the whole 1994-2010 period.  We omit (and
17:586:50388:22:22:70:524:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hence  standardize  for)  the  year  1998  which  is  the  last  observation  before  the  signing  of  the
17:587:50495:22:62:70:404:231:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:AFMP. This is implemented by estimating the following specification:
17:588:50563:62:0:102:199:169:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:A:ym,t=αm+αt+
17:589:50574:0:27:206:223:183:8:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f15:C:2010∑

17:600:50728:28:0:79:495:65:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:23From the list of industries, we dropped the industry ‘Recycling’ which was not available in all years.
18:601:50834:0:22:87:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The variableI(year=t) is an indicator dummy equal to one in yeartand zero in every
18:602:50916:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:other year, while the other variables are as defined in equation (2).  We include year dummies,
18:603:51011:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:B:αtand  municipality  dummies,αm.   Since  we  omit  the  interaction  term  for  year  1998  in  the
18:604:51111:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:summation, the other coefficients will represent the difference relative to 1998.  The estimates of
18:605:51210:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the coefficientsγd1,tfor each year between 1994 and 2010 are the parameters of interest as they
18:606:51305:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:represent the differential of outcome between the most intensely treated group (municipalities at
18:607:51402:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:0−10 minutes from the border) and the control group (municipalities at 30 plus minutes from
18:608:51493:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the Border).  Another advantage is that using this specification we can test whether the year
18:609:51586:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:estimates are consistent with the assumptions of our identification strategy.  Specifically, as the
18:610:51685:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:impact of the policy should be zero prior to the date it was announced, and as we are assuming
18:611:51779:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that the control municipalities represent a valid counter-factual for the treated ones, we should
18:612:51876:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:find thatγd1t= 0, fort <1998.  Namely, for our identification strategy to work there should
18:613:51967:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be no significant different in outcomes between treatment and control municipalities before the
18:614:52062:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:policy.  If the policy had any impact on any outcome,ymt, then we should find a positive effect,
18:615:52158:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:possibly after the signing of the agreement in 1999 or after full liberalization in 2004,  on the
18:616:52255:22:22:70:523:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipalities  next  to  the  border.   The  estimates  for  the  1999−2004  years  provide  evidence
18:617:52357:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of an effect during theTransitionphase, while the estimates of the post-2004 coefficients test
18:618:52451:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whether there was an effect duringFull LiberalizationPhase.  The coefficientsγd1,tfort≥1999
18:619:52542:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:will reveal the policy effect on the most intensely treated municipalities andγd2,tandγd3,twould
18:620:52638:22:45:70:465:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:reveal the impact, if there is any, in moderately and weakly treated municipalities.
18:621:52722:45:34:70:374:312:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:4    Policy and the Intensity of CBW Flows
18:622:52764:34:29:70:249:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:4.1    Changes in CBW Supply
18:623:52792:29:22:70:524:249:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Table 2 shows the estimates for the coefficients of interest from equation 2 when the dependent
18:624:52887:22:21:70:524:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variable is the number of CBW as a share of total employment in year 1998, which is kept fixed
18:625:52981:21:22:70:524:206:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:as to avoid spurious effects due to changes in native employment.  As CBW comprise the group
18:626:53073:22:22:70:524:184:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whose presence is directly affected by the policy, Table 2 establishes how the policy affected the
18:627:53171:22:22:70:524:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:treatment across municipalities in the two phases.  In the first three rows we see the coefficients
18:628:53270:22:22:70:524:140:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on  the  interaction  of  the  “Transition  Phase”  with  the  three  distance  dummies,  namelyβFd1,
