34:1180:103538:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firms:  the  effects  they  found  were  particularly  strong  in  high-tech  firms.   Interestingly,  when
34:1181:103645:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:we separate by skill, the positive wage effects in this sector seem stronger for middle- and less-
34:1182:103743:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educated  native  workers  who  are  likely  to  be  complementary  to  the  technical  skills  of  CBW.
34:1183:103847:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:When  we  break  the  estimates  further  down  by  education  groups,  we  find  a  positive  wage  ef-
34:1184:103951:22:22:70:523:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:fect in the order 5.7 percentage points at 0−10 minutes from the border for highly-educated
34:1185:104042:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in  knowledge-intensive  services.   To  the  contrary,  less-educated  workers  in  services  may  have
34:1186:104146:22:22:70:422:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:experience a wage loss of around three percentage points near the border.
34:1187:104219:22:22:87:524:116:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Table 8 Panels A-D, shows a set of industry-specific coefficients, similar to those shown in
34:1188:104311:22:22:70:524:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Table  7,  on  log  of  hours  worked  by  natives.   These  captures  possible  shifts  in  labor  supply
34:1189:104417:22:0:70:524:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:by  natives  in  response  to  CBW  across  those  sectors.   Expansion  and  increased  productivity
35:1190:104520:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:at  the  sector  level  may  imply  a  larger  labor  supply  of  native  workers.   While  the  coefficients
35:1191:104629:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:are mostly non-significant,  there is some evidence of a positive effect on the hours worked of
35:1192:104724:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:high-educated  in  high-tech  manufacturing  and  of  less-skilled  natives  in  services  that  are  not
35:1193:104829:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:knowledge-intensive.   This  last  effect  may  be  driven  by  positive  job-multiplier  effects  (as  de-
35:1194:104936:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:scribed by Moretti (2010)) on local, low-skill services, and support companies (e.g.  hotel, food,
35:1195:105034:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:hospitality industries) attracted by the growth of high tech manufacturing and services.  The
35:1196:105127:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:positive effect on employment and zero (or even negative) effect on the wages of low-educated
35:1197:105220:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:natives in this sector is consistent with a highly elastic labor supply for these jobs that require
35:1198:105319:22:22:70:382:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:very generic skills, and a possible negative selection in the sector.
35:1199:105388:22:21:87:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In all the existing regressions we have focused on private sector employment.  it is however
35:1200:105480:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:interesting to mention another possible margin of adjustment.  In Appendix Table A8 we show
35:1201:105571:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the impact on employment in public sector workers.  These are estimated using data from the
35:1202:105662:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Swiss Business Census (BC), a different database, which includes, differently from the rest of the
35:1203:105760:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:paper, public-sector workers.  A significant effect shown in this table is the tendency of native
35:1204:105857:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers to move towards public sector jobs in response to CBW. There is a significant, albeit
35:1205:105950:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:small, shift of about one percent of native employment moving from the private to the public
35:1206:106042:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sector  after  the  liberalization.   This  transition  could  be  an  additional  channel  through  which
35:1207:106148:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:natives  protected  their  wages  from  immigrant  competition,  as  native  have  easier  access  than
35:1208:106251:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:immigrants to public jobs.  We do not know of other studies that analyze this margin, which
35:1209:106342:22:38:70:292:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can be important in some European countries.
35:1210:106386:38:29:70:242:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:6.4    Effect on Firm Creation
35:1211:106416:29:22:70:524:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The positive productivity effect from CBW, consistent with higher wages and employment of
35:1212:106505:22:21:70:524:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:natives, and particularly clear in high tech manufacturing and knowledge intensive service sec-
35:1213:106600:21:22:70:524:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tor, may also derive from a complementarity of these workers with capital investments.  Their
35:1214:106693:22:22:70:524:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:presence,  and  the  perspective  of  hiring  them,  may  have  attracted  new  establishments  in  the
35:1215:106796:22:22:70:524:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:region  near  the  border,  producing  the  growth  of  employment  and  wages  we  observed.   The
35:1216:106895:22:22:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:prospect of hiring the right type of workers can be a very strong attractor for firms and a key
35:1217:106990:22:22:70:524:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:driver of agglomeration economies (as in Moretti, 2004).  In Table 9 we consider the creation of
35:1218:107086:22:22:70:524:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:new establishment, as a share of total establishment in the sector in 1998, during the Transition
35:1219:107183:22:22:70:524:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:phase and during the Full Liberalization phase, in the four sectors considered above (high- and
35:1220:107278:22:22:70:524:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:low-tech manufacturing in columns (1) and (2), and sectors that were and were not knowledge-
35:1221:107370:22:0:70:524:71:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensive in columns (3) and (4)).  The estimates show the largest positive firm creation effects
36:1222:107469:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:during the Full Liberalization period (coefficients of the ”FREE” variable).  It appears that such
36:1223:107567:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firm-creation was quite widespread across sectors, although stronger in high-tech manufacturing
36:1224:107662:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and in Knowledge-intensive services, in line with the previous results.  The aggregate effect is
36:1225:107758:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:an additional creation of new establishments by 3.4 percent in the bin closest to the border, by
36:1226:107854:22:22:70:452:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2.8 percent in the bin at 20−30 minutes and a little bit less in the 10−20 bin.
36:1227:107933:22:22:87:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:During the Transition we also find a (smaller) effect of between one and two percent higher
36:1228:108024:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firm-creation in aggregate.  This is consistent with the idea that anticipation of a larger supply
36:1229:108122:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  CBW  may  have  attracted  new  investment  and  new  firms  already  in  the  transition.   The
36:1230:108222:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sector distribution of the effects during the transition shows noisier and less precisely estimated
36:1231:108321:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:coefficients.   It  suggests  that  the  high-tech  manufacturing  and  service  sector  experienced  the
36:1232:108426:21:22:70:508:555:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:largest entry of new establishments relative to the initial number of firms in these sectors.43
36:1233:108521:22:22:87:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Summarizing the role of different channels we have shown that internal migration and mo-
36:1234:108609:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:bility have not played a particularly relevant role in response to the opening to CBW. Instead,
36:1235:108704:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:upgrading of natives to managerial positions, gains in productivity in high-tech and knowledge
36:1236:108798:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensive  services,  and  attraction  and  birth  of  new  firms  have  been  stimulated  by  the  policy,
36:1237:108905:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:especially  during  the  phase  of  full  mobility.   Together  these  channels  are  consistent  with  the
36:1238:109012:22:38:70:479:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:wage increase of highly skilled natives estimated after allowing free mobility of CBW.
36:1239:109098:38:29:70:340:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:6.5    Comparison with Recent Similar Studies
36:1240:109143:29:22:70:524:356:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Before concluding,  we systematically compare our results with those of two recent papers re-
36:1241:109236:22:22:70:524:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:lated to this one and point out similarities and differences.  The first study from Ruffner and
36:1242:109331:22:22:70:524:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Siegenthaler (2016) was developed concurrently to this paper and focuses on the same episode of
36:1243:109426:22:22:70:524:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:liberalization in Switzerland.  Ruffner and Siegenthaler (2016) use firm-level data and focus on
36:1244:109522:22:21:70:524:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firm outcomes:  labor productivity, sales, R&D investments, innovation, and firm entry and exit
36:1245:109617:21:22:70:524:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after CBW liberalization.  They provide results that are complementary to those presented in
36:1246:109709:22:22:70:524:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this paper.  First, they show that firms close to the border experienced an increase in aggregate
36:1247:109806:22:22:70:524:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment and an expansion in sales and a mild increase in productivity post-liberalization.
36:1248:109899:22:22:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The authors also document that firms expressing worries about shortages of highly-skilled work-
36:1249:109994:22:22:70:524:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ers  in  the  pre-liberalization  period  (via  a  survey)  experienced  larger  increase  in  sales  and  in
36:1250:110103:22:22:70:524:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:value-added per workers following the liberalization.  This confirms that the expansion of CBW
36:1251:110197:22:22:70:524:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:supply may have facilitated growth, investment, and productivity gains.  Second, firms that ben-
36:1252:110293:22:16:70:524:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:efited most with respect to productivity and growth were those in the high-tech sector, larger
36:1253:110387:16:15:79:524:77:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:43These results complement the findings of Ruffner and Siegenthaler (2016) who also find positive effects on
36:1254:110495:15:0:70:354:62:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:firm entry and no robust effects on firm exit close to the Swiss border.
37:1255:110569:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firms, and those previously dependent on cross-border workers.  This result is consistent with
37:1256:110663:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the stronger positive wage effects we find on high-tech manufacturing workers (Table 7).  Third,
37:1257:110759:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Ruffner and Siegenthaler (2016) find that firms also experienced larger innovation rates, larger
37:1258:110855:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment shares in R&D, and more entry of new establishments as a consequence of CBW
37:1259:110941:22:22:70:135:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:liberalization.
37:1260:110956:22:22:87:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Our  paper,  on  the  other  hand,  goes  much  more  in  depth  into  the  analysis  of  the  labor
37:1261:111056:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:market dynamics triggered by the opening of the border.  First, it shows that CBW were highly
37:1262:111149:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educated and did not crowd out other immigrants, but increased total foreign-born employment,
37:1263:111242:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:especially of highly-skilled.  Second we show that they triggered dynamics through which highly-
37:1264:111338:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:educated local workers were more likely to become top managers and stay in the municipality,
37:1265:111430:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:while  internal  mobility  of  Swiss  workers  was  not  affected  much.   Third  our  analysis  suggests
37:1266:111535:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:that,  possibly  because  of  a  positive  local  job  multiplier  (as  in  Moretti  (2010))  from  CBW,
37:1267:111639:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  employment  and  wages  in  high-tech  manufacturing  and  knowledge-intensive  services  was
37:1268:111737:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:positively  affected.   What  both  studies  suggest  is  the  fact  that  the  absorption  of  new  CBW
37:1269:111841:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after 2004 took place via job and firm creation and increased productivity, innovation, and total
37:1270:111938:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment.  Our analysis also unveils a more detailed account of who gained and who lost from
37:1271:112032:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  opening  of  the  border  among  Swiss  workers.   Older,  highly-educated,  male  workers  with
37:1272:112133:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:longer tenure  were  the  main beneficiaries,  as they  took managerial jobs  in response to CBW
37:1273:112229:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:inflow.   Importantly,  these  positive  effects  may  be  connected  to  the  fact  that  the  new  CBW
37:1274:112333:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:were highly skilled, that the growth in their supply had a transition period (1999-2004), during
37:1275:112429:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:which firms could prepare their adjustment.  The fact that we document also some positive firm
37:1276:112523:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:creation during the transition phase confirms this conjecture.  Hence, in evaluating the impact
37:1277:112618:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of immigration policy changes and the consequences of the ensuing inflow of immigrants, this
37:1278:112710:21:22:70:245:270:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:episode may be particularly useful.44
37:1279:112747:22:22:87:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A second paper with important similarity to ours, especially for the type of policy considered,
37:1280:112842:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:is  Dustmann,  Sch ̈onberg  and  Stuhler  (2017).   The  authors  analyze  the  effect  of  a  temporary
37:1281:112946:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:agreement allowing the free access of cross-border workers from the Czech Republic to Germany
37:1282:113039:22:22:70:524:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:between 1991 and 1993.  This agreement followed the fall of Communism in Eastern Europe,
37:1283:113127:22:22:70:524:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  increased  the  presence  of  Czech  workers  in  the  bordering  German  regions.   Similarly  to
37:1284:113230:22:16:70:524:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the  Swiss  case,  the  effect  on  labor  supply  was  highly  concentrated  near  the  border  because
37:1285:113334:16:15:79:524:122:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:44It is somewhat harder to reconcile our results with the initial policy report by Losa, Bigotta and Gonzales
37:1286:113443:15:11:70:524:107:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(2012) that looked at the employment and wage effects of removing barriers on CBW. That paper applied a simple
37:1287:113553:11:11:70:524:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:difference-in-difference approach between border and non-border regions and it focused on the short run effects
37:1288:113664:11:11:70:524:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:(2 years after the policy).  Such an approach can incur significant noise and measurement error as we documented
37:1289:113776:11:11:70:524:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:that the changes in CBW took a few years since 2004 and that only the municipalities closest to the border (rather
37:1290:113890:11:0:70:392:63:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:than the whole border region) experienced a significant increase in their supply.
38:1291:113973:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of the commuting requirement.  Yet,  Dustmann,  Sch ̈onberg and Stuhler (2017) find that this
38:1292:114066:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:inflow was associated with a large decline in the employment of old, unskilled Germans and a
38:1293:114158:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:larger decline in wages of younger workers.  The authors explain these differences with different
38:1294:114255:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:degrees of rigidity of wages and elasticity of supply of different age groups.  Our findings are
38:1295:114351:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:particularly interesting in light of these results.  However, it must be born in mind that there are
38:1296:114451:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:three main differences between the German set-up and the Swiss case.  First, the Czech inflow
38:1297:114544:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:was mainly composed of less-educated workers hired in relatively manual-intensive occupations.
38:1298:114638:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Second,  it  was  unexpected  and  not  planned  years  in  advance.   Third,  it  wastemporary,  and
38:1299:114739:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:perceived as such, and it was reversed in 1993.  Each of these features may have reduced the
38:1300:114831:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:response  margin  of  native  workers  and  firms,  limiting  the  ability  to  absorb  the  new  workers
38:1301:114936:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  hence  these  differences  may  contribute  to  explain  the  different  labor  market  effects  on
38:1302:115040:22:22:70:524:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:natives:  negative in the   case of Dustmann, Sch ̈onberg and Stuhler (2017), and positive in our
38:1303:115137:22:22:70:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:case.  Dustmann, Sch ̈onberg and Stuhler (2017) also discuss the main channels of adjustment of
38:1304:115232:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:native employment, which seems to be a reduction of other natives moving to those regions.  This
38:1305:115328:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:seems plausible because the region near the border with the Czech Republic, due to the turmoil
38:1306:115422:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:created by the end of Communism, may have experienced more economic uncertainty and less
38:1307:115510:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:growth than other regions around 1991-1992.  The Swiss experiment, instead, took place around
38:1308:115603:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:2004, a period in which the countries near the border were not experiencing significant economic
38:1309:115699:22:22:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:transitions.   Hence  it  may  be  a  cleaner  case  to  isolate  the  effect  of  apermanent  immigration
38:1310:115805:22:22:70:524:357:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:B:reformon local labor markets, avoiding other economic spillover effects from across the border.
38:1311:115900:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Also  the  high  skills  of  immigrants  and  the  different  horizon  of  the  policy  may  be  crucial  to
38:1312:116008:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:explain our positive results on native wages.  More generally, however, we cannot make a strong
38:1313:116103:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:statement  about  which  feature  of  the  Swiss  set-up  generated  the  difference  for  the  effect  on
38:1314:116209:21:46:70:428:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes we observe vis-`a-vis the German-Czech set-up in the early 1990s.
38:1315:116283:46:33:70:171:224:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:7    Conclusion
38:1316:116298:33:22:70:524:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:In  this  paper,  we  analyze  the  effect  of  liberalization  of  labor  market  access  for  cross-border
38:1317:116406:22:22:70:524:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers,  implemented  in  Switzerland  between  1999  and  2007,  on  the  labor  supply  of  foreign
38:1318:116508:22:21:70:524:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers  and  on  native  labor  market  outcomes.   We  adopt  a  difference-in-difference  approach
38:1319:116609:21:22:70:524:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and we exploit the fact that the availability of cross-border workers strongly depended on the
38:1320:116703:22:22:70:524:104:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:commuting  time  from  the  national  border,  as  these  workers  resided  abroad  and  commuted
38:1321:116800:22:22:70:524:82:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to  work  in  Switzerland.   After  showing  that  the  introduction  of  free  labor  market  access  for
38:1322:116906:22:0:70:524:60:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:these workers in 2004 produced a progressive and significant increase in their employment in
39:1323:117000:0:22:70:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipalities within 0−20 minutes of travel time from the border, but very little effect beyond
39:1324:117096:22:22:70:524:752:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:30  minutes  from  the  border,  we  analyze  their  impact  on  labor  market  outcomes  of  natives.
39:1325:117198:22:22:70:524:730:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:We find that, in the aggregate, natives in municipalities within the 0−20 minute range from
39:1326:117289:22:22:70:524:708:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the border did not experience any differential change in average log wages, log employment, or
39:1327:117383:22:22:70:524:686:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:log hours after the liberalization relative to natives in similar municipalities farther away from
39:1328:117481:22:22:70:524:664:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the border.  However, this insignificant post-liberalization change in averages masks a positive
39:1329:117577:22:22:70:524:642:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and significant change in the wages of highly-educated natives.  This effect is the strongest and
39:1330:117674:22:22:70:524:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:most robust estimate in the paper.  We also find a positive but less robust and only marginally
39:1331:117769:22:22:70:524:598:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:significant positive change on hours worked by less-educated natives in the region near the border
39:1332:117867:22:21:70:524:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:after liberalization.  To better understand these results, we analyze several margins and channels
39:1333:117965:21:22:70:524:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of adjustment for native workers that may explain the positive wage change for highly-educated
39:1334:118059:22:22:70:522:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:natives, which is not consistent with a increase in supply in the canonical labor market model.
39:1335:118154:22:22:87:524:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:We rule out internal migration as a significant adjustment mechanism, and provide suggestive
39:1336:118246:22:22:70:524:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:evidence  on  three  interesting  mechanisms  that  seem  to  be  at  work  in  response  to  the  higher
39:1337:118351:22:22:70:524:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:supply  of  CBW.  First,  we  find  evidence  that  highly-educated  natives,  and  particularly  older
39:1338:118454:22:22:70:524:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and  more  senior  workers,  became  more  likely  to  take  top  management  positions.   Second  we
39:1339:118555:22:22:70:524:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:find  positive  productivity  (wage)  effects  in  the  high-tech  manufacturing  sector  and  in  skilled
39:1340:118661:22:22:70:524:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:services, where the employment of skilled CBW increased the most.  Third, we find more new
39:1341:118751:22:22:70:355:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:firm creation in the border regions after Full Liberalization.
39:1342:118813:22:22:87:524:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Overall,  this  suggests  that  the  CBW  produced  positive  effects  on  local,  highly-educated
39:1343:118911:22:22:70:524:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:workers, through both a complementarity and a productivity channel, by pushing some of them
39:1344:119002:22:22:70:524:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to managerial and high-pay occupations and by attracting capital and new firms in knowledge-
39:1345:119094:22:21:70:524:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:intensive  sectors.   The  variety  of  responses  to  immigration  makes  clear  that  a  simple  static,
39:1346:119200:21:22:70:524:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:partial-effects model of fixed demand and change in supply does not work well in explaining the
39:1347:119295:22:22:70:524:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:effect of immigration in this case.  Rather, different types of complementarity, gains from special-
39:1348:119395:22:22:70:524:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:ization, and productivity effects are at work when firms and workers adapt.  Most importantly,
39:1349:119489:22:22:70:524:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:B:this paper is one of the few to directly analyze the labor market consequences of apermanent
39:1350:119581:22:0:70:523:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:andcompletelabor market liberalization policy for some foreign workers in local labor markets.

70:2520:181657:0:34:70:206:774:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:B    Data Appendix
70:2521:181675:34:20:70:341:740:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:B.1    Measurement of employment transitions
70:2522:181719:20:13:70:524:720:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:To calculate transition rates, we use the Swiss Labor Force Survey (SLFS) and exploit its rolling
70:2523:181816:13:13:70:524:707:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:panel structure, i.e.  individuals are called back in the SLFS up to 4 consecutive years after their
70:2524:181916:13:13:70:524:694:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:first interview.  However, for our purpose only the panel of two consecutive years is of reasonable
70:2525:182015:13:13:70:524:681:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:size.  Using information on the labor force status and municipality of work in the previous year
70:2526:182111:13:13:70:524:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of any individual worker, we can decompose total employment of groupGin a municipalitym,
70:2527:182199:13:15:70:144:655:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:B:EGm,t, as follows
70:2528:182216:15:26:221:524:640:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:A:EGm,t=STAYGm,t−1,t+INGm,t−1,t(4)
70:2529:182248:26:13:70:523:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whereSTAYGm,t−1,tis the number of individuals who stayed employed in municipalitymbetween
70:2530:182337:13:13:70:524:601:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f10:B:the previous yeart−1 and this yeartand those who moved into employment in municipalitym
70:2531:182424:13:16:70:523:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:during the same period,INGm,t−1,t.  Inflows can be further disaggregated into inflows from other
70:2532:182520:16:13:70:524:572:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipalities,ING,−m→mm,t−1,tin the treated border region (below 30 minutes travel time from the
70:2533:182617:13:15:70:524:559:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border) or from municipalities in the control region (in the border region above 30 minutes from
70:2534:182713:15:13:70:523:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the border).  Inflow can also come from non-employment,ING,NE→mm,t−1,t.  In a similar fashion, we
70:2535:182810:13:30:70:420:531:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:can decompose the current total employment with a forward perspective:
70:2536:182880:30:33:216:524:501:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:A:EGm,t=STAYGm,t,t+1+OUTGm,t,t+1(5)
70:2537:182913:33:13:70:523:468:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:whereSTAYGm,t,t+1andOUTGm,t,t+1constitute the individuals staying employed inmor leaving
70:2538:183001:13:13:70:524:455:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:employment inmfrom this yeartto next yeart+ 1, respectively.  Analogously, outflows can
70:2539:183088:13:16:70:524:442:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:be decomposed into outflows to employment in other areas,OUTG,m→−mm,t,t+1(treatment or control
70:2540:183182:16:14:70:303:426:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:regions), and to non-employment,OUTG,m→NEm,t,t+1.
70:2541:183231:14:13:87:524:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Lastly, the sum of inflow minus outflow constitute thenet changeof total employment of a
70:2542:183319:13:30:70:208:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f10:B:groupGin a municipalitym
70:2543:183343:30:31:166:524:369:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:A:NETGm,t,t+1=INGm,t,t+1−OUTGm,t,t+1=EGm,t+1−EGm,t(6)
70:2544:183394:31:13:87:524:338:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:As we only have information on the municipality of work in the years 1996 to 2009 in the
70:2545:183482:13:13:70:524:325:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:SLFS,  we  can  calculate  inflow  rates  from  1997  to  2009  and  outflow  rates  from  1996  to  2008,
70:2546:183588:13:14:70:524:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:respectively,  by  calculating  the  likelihood  of  each  category  in  a  municipality-year-education
70:2547:183691:14:16:70:524:298:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:group  cell,  e.g.   in  the  first  year  the  outflow  rate  isOUTGm,96,97/Em,96and  the  inflow  rate  is
70:2548:183799:16:14:70:543:282:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f11:C:INGm,96,97/Em,97.45The net inflow, in turn, is calculated asNETGm,96,97/ ̃Em,96,97≡INGm,96,97/Em,97−
70:2549:183899:14:14:70:159:268:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:B:OUTGm,96,97/Em,96.
70:2550:183917:14:13:87:524:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:For  consistency  in  the  regression  analysis,  inflow  rates  are  always  deferred  one  year  back
70:2551:184020:13:13:70:524:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and, thus, are used for the same years as the outflow rates in the regression analysis between
70:2552:184114:13:13:70:524:228:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:1996 and 2008 where each year refers to the flow between the current year and the next year.
70:2553:184206:13:58:70:347:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Cells are weighted using their total employment in a year.
70:2554:184264:58:34:70:506:157:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:C    More Details on Reform and the Institutional Framework
70:2555:184323:34:20:70:424:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:C.1    Bilateral agreements between Switzerland and the EU
70:2556:184381:20:13:70:524:103:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:The  bilateral  agreements  I,  signed  in  June  1999  between  Switzerland  and  the  EU,  included,
70:2557:184483:13:14:70:508:90:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:apart from the free movement policy, six other liberalization agreements (Bundesrat, 1999):
70:2558:184574:14:0:79:434:76:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:45In so doing, we use the panel survey weights provided for the OFS for the SLFS data.
71:2559:184662:0:14:87:524:774:11:g_d0_f39:11:g_d0_f4:A:•The agreement ontechnical barriers to trade(or ‘‘Mutual Recognition Agreement’’) aimed
71:2560:184749:14:13:98:523:760:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:at the mutual recognition of conformity tests for a wide range of industrial products.46
71:2561:184837:13:14:98:524:747:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:This implies, that the declaration of conformity from a Swiss test centre is also valid in
71:2562:184927:14:22:98:429:733:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:the EU and vice versa reducing the time and costs for trading goods.
71:2563:184995:22:14:87:524:711:11:g_d0_f39:11:g_d0_f4:A:•The agreement onagricultural productsfacilitates trade of particular agricultural products
71:2564:185086:14:22:98:451:697:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:by reducing customs duties and non-tariff barriers for selected products.47
71:2565:185161:22:14:87:524:675:11:g_d0_f39:11:g_d0_f4:A:•With the agreement onoverland  transport, the Swiss government raised the weight limit
71:2566:185248:14:14:98:524:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:of heavy goods vehicles gradually to 40 metric tonnes after 2002 and introduced a tax on
71:2567:185336:14:13:98:524:647:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:heavy vehicles, providing incentives for transalpine freight to shift from road to rail.  The
71:2568:185429:13:14:98:524:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:agreement oncivil aviationallowed reciprocal access to aviation markets including landing
71:2569:185518:14:22:98:298:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:rights and was fully implemented in 2002.
71:2570:185559:22:14:87:524:598:11:g_d0_f39:11:g_d0_f4:A:•The agreement onpublic procurementextends the WTO rules and requires larger tenders
71:2571:185643:14:13:98:524:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:by  municipalities  and  certain  sectors  (e.g.   telecommunication,  rail  transport  and  water
71:2572:185741:13:23:98:351:571:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:A:and energy) to be subject to compulsory tendering.48
71:2573:185793:23:13:87:524:548:11:g_d0_f39:11:g_d0_f4:A:•The agreement onscientific and technological cooperationallows Swiss researchers to par-
71:2574:185882:13:25:98:313:535:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:ticipate in EU research framework programs.
71:2575:185925:25:14:87:524:510:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:In an assessment to which degree each of the bilateral agreements facilitated market access
71:2576:186016:14:13:70:524:496:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:for a particular industry, B ̈uhler, Helm and Lechner (2011) expect the manufacturing industries
71:2577:186112:13:13:70:524:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to be most affected and, to a lesser extent, some service industries (particularly vehicle trade
71:2578:186208:13:13:70:524:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:and wholesale and commission trade).  Based on these classification, B ̈uhler, Helm and Lechner
71:2579:186303:13:13:70:524:457:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(2011) find that employment growth was 1-2 percentage points larger among affected firms after
71:2580:186397:13:13:70:335:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the implementation of the bilateral agreements in 2002.
71:2581:186452:13:13:87:524:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Based on an assessment to which degree the entire package of bilateral agreements liberalised
71:2582:186545:13:13:70:524:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:access  to  the  EU  market  for  a  particular  2-digit  industry,  B ̈uhler,  Helm  and  Lechner  (2011)
71:2583:186651:13:13:70:398:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:classify firms into three groups of high, low and non-affected sectors.
71:2584:186722:13:13:87:524:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:A  second  set  of  bilateral  agreements  (II)  where  signed  in  October  2004  and  approved  in
71:2585:186822:13:13:70:524:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a  referendum  with  55%  favorable  votes  on  June  5,  2005.49The  most  relevant  agreement  for
71:2586:186922:13:14:70:524:366:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:our study is theSchengenagreement which abolished the control of individuals at the border
71:2587:187012:14:13:70:524:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:traveling.  Yet, persons can still be controlled at the border and border guards remain at the
71:2588:187106:13:13:70:524:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:border as Switzerland does not belong to the EU customs union (or in the event of an initial
71:2589:187198:13:16:70:467:326:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:B:suspicion of a criminal offence.  Schengen became effective on December 12, 2008.50
71:2590:187281:16:14:79:524:310:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:46Conformity tests certify that a product complies with the local regulation (e.g.  for toys) and can be offered on
71:2591:187396:14:11:70:524:296:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:its market.  Since 1992, Switzerland has adapted its regulation to those of the EU to large degrees.  This agreement
71:2592:187512:11:11:70:524:285:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:covers a wide range of products including machines, printers, medical products, motor vehicles, tractors, measuring
71:2593:187627:11:7:70:407:274:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:instruments, telecommunication devices, and, since March 2008, building materials.
71:2594:187709:7:15:79:524:267:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:47Customs duties were reduced for cheese, fruits and vegetables, horticulture, meat and wine. Non-tariff barriers
71:2595:187822:15:11:70:524:252:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:reductions aimed, inter alia, at wine and spirits, organic agriculture, pest control and crop protection, fodder and
71:2596:187938:11:11:70:524:241:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:seeds.  The reduction of customs duties was implemented fully for most goods on June 1 2002.  For cheese, the
71:2597:188047:11:7:70:397:230:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:reductions were introduced step-wise with a full liberalisation after June 1, 2007.
71:2598:188130:7:15:79:524:223:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:48Public tenders are required only above a certain minimum amount, which is approximately CHF 10 million for
71:2599:188238:15:11:70:524:208:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:buildings, CHF 250’000 for goods and services provided to the Confederation and 380’000 for goods and services
71:2600:188348:11:7:70:445:197:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:provided to municipalities and cantons.  This agreement was implemented fully in June 2002.
71:2601:188439:7:15:79:524:190:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:49The bilateral agreements II included agreements on border controls and asylum (Schengen & Dublin, opera-
71:2602:188545:15:11:70:524:175:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:tional December 12, 2008), the taxation of savings (operational July 1, 2005), fight against fraud (operational April
71:2603:188662:11:11:70:524:164:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:8, 2009), environmental cooperation (effective April 1, 2006), liberalisation of processed agricultural goods (effec-
71:2604:188779:11:11:70:524:153:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:tive March 30, 2005), film promotion (effective April 1, 2006), pensions (effective May 31, 2005) and cooperation
71:2605:188892:11:7:70:239:142:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:with statistics (effective January 1, 2007).
71:2606:188936:7:15:79:524:135:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:50The Schengen agreement also entails increased control at the external border (e.g.  airports), a common visa
71:2607:189046:15:0:70:320:120:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:policy and cooperation between the police and justice system.
72:2608:189109:0:29:70:448:774:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:C.2    Taxation and Social Benefits of Immigrants in Switzerland
72:2609:189173:29:20:70:225:745:11:g_d0_f40:11:g_d0_f40:C:C.2.1    Resident immigrants
72:2610:189201:20:13:70:524:725:11:g_d0_f40:11:g_d0_f4:B:TaxationTaxation of foreign residents in Switzerland depends on the income level and the
72:2611:189289:13:14:70:524:712:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:residency status.51Foreign residents with a short-term (B or L) permit with an annual gross
72:2612:189380:14:13:70:524:698:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:income  below  120’000  CHF are  subject  to  aspecial  tax  schemewith  ‘taxation  at the  source’
72:2613:189479:13:13:70:524:685:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:(Quellensteuer).52Taxes  are  subtracted  directly  from  the  salary  by  the  employer  depending
72:2614:189578:13:13:70:524:672:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on household characteristics (marital status, number of children), the canton of living and the
72:2615:189673:13:13:70:524:659:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:income level (progressivity).  For these individuals, a canton-wide tax rate applies which is the
72:2616:189770:13:13:70:524:646:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:weighted  average  of  municipality  tax  rates  within  a  canton.   Thus,  these  individuals  face  no
72:2617:189875:13:13:70:524:633:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:variation in their tax burden within a canton.  After staying in Switzerland at least five years of
72:2618:189974:13:13:70:490:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:uninterruptedly, short-term permit holders can apply for a permanent residency permit.
72:2619:190060:13:13:87:524:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:Permanent  residency  holders  and  short-term  permit  holders  with  a  gross  income  above
72:2620:190154:13:13:70:524:594:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:120’000 CHF are subject to theordinary taxation scheme.  The ordinary taxation scheme con-
72:2621:190244:13:13:70:524:581:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:sists  of  three  layers  with  income  taxes  set  at  the  federal,  the  cantonal  and  the  municipality
72:2622:190352:13:14:70:524:568:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:level.  The federal and cantonal tax schedules determine how progressive taxes are.  In turn, the
72:2623:190449:14:13:70:524:554:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:municipal tax rate is defined as the cantonal tax rate times a tax multiplier (Steuerfuss) set by
72:2624:190546:13:13:70:524:541:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:the municipality.  Thus, the overall tax liability depends on household characteristics (marital
72:2625:190642:13:28:70:470:528:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:status and children), the income level (progressivity) and the municipality of living.
72:2626:190728:28:13:70:524:500:11:g_d0_f40:11:g_d0_f4:B:Social benefitsIn general,unemployment benefitscan be claimed in the country where indi-
72:2627:190816:13:13:70:524:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:viduals have been employed last.  Individuals without employment are allowed to enter and stay
72:2628:190910:13:13:70:524:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:in Switzerland conditional on having a health insurance and having sufficient financial funds.
72:2629:191004:13:13:70:524:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:Individuals  looking  for  a  job  can  stay  for  up  to  six  months  conditional  on  having  sufficient
72:2630:191111:13:14:70:524:448:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:financial  funds  (EDA,  2015).   Foreign  residents  with  a  short-term  permit  below  one  year  (L
72:2631:191214:14:13:70:524:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:or seasonal workers prior to 2002) are entitled for unemployment benefits during the duration
72:2632:191307:13:13:70:524:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of  their  permit  conditional  on  having  contributed  at  least  for  six  months.   After  a  transition
72:2633:191415:13:13:70:524:408:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:period of seven years after 2002, short-term permit holder are entitled for benefits like natives
72:2634:191512:13:13:70:524:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:conditional on a minimum number of contribution months to which also contributions in other
72:2635:191603:13:13:70:524:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:countries are taken into account.  For foreign residents with a long-term permit of more than one
72:2636:191700:13:13:70:521:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:year past contribution months are taken into account already prior to 2002 (Bundesrat, 1999).
72:2637:191793:13:13:87:524:356:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f4:A:Other  benefits, like health, accident, disability insurance, pensions schemes largely depend
72:2638:191886:13:37:70:492:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:on the country of employment and the time during which contribution have been payed.
72:2639:191970:37:21:70:229:306:11:g_d0_f40:11:g_d0_f40:C:C.2.2    Cross-border workers
72:2640:191999:21:13:70:524:285:11:g_d0_f40:11:g_d0_f4:B:TaxationCross-border workers are also subject to thespecial tax schemewith taxation at the
72:2641:192089:13:13:70:524:272:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:source.53The introduction of the free movement of persons policy after June 1, 2002, created
72:2642:192181:13:13:70:524:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:a new category of cross-border workers which were allowed to commute back only on a weekly
72:2643:192271:13:13:70:524:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:basis (rather than daily before). Yet, individuals in this new category (‘Wochenaufenthalter’) are
72:2644:192369:13:13:70:524:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:similarly taxed as cross-border workers prior to the free movement policy.  The actual details of
72:2645:192466:13:13:70:524:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:this taxation depend on the canton of work and the country of living due to bilateral agreements
72:2646:192562:13:13:70:524:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:of Switzerland with each of the neighbouring countries for the taxation of cross-border workers.
72:2647:192658:13:13:87:524:194:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:CBWs fromGermanyare subject to taxation at their place of residency. Cantons are allowed
72:2648:192746:13:13:70:524:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to tax these individuals at the source at a maximum rate of 4.5% of the gross income.54This
72:2649:192837:13:13:70:524:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:tax is accounted for when calculating the tax burden in Germany.  If a CBW does not return
72:2650:192927:13:14:70:524:155:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:to her residency on more than 60 working days, she gets fully taxed at the source like resident
72:2651:193022:14:15:70:127:141:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:immigrants.
72:2652:193033:15:11:79:380:126:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:51This information is largely based on Schmidheiny and Slotwinski (2015).
72:2653:193106:11:15:79:524:115:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:52This threshold is at an gross annual income of 500’000 in the canton Geneva.  Individuals who are married to
72:2654:193216:15:7:70:493:100:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:a Swiss resident or a permanent foreign resident are subject to the ordinary tax scheme explained below.
72:2655:193320:7:11:79:278:93:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:53This paragraph is largely based on SSK (2009).
72:2656:193368:11:15:79:524:82:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:F:54This  taxation  scheme  is  subject  to  a  proof  of  residency  (Ans ̈assigkeitsbescheinigung)  of  the  CBW  to  her
72:2657:193489:15:0:70:109:67:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:F:employer.
73:2658:193500:0:13:87:524:774:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A:The taxation of CBW fromFrancedepends on the canton of work.  CBWs working in border
73:2659:193584:13:13:70:524:761:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:B:cantons (SO, BS, BL, VD, VS, NE and JU) and the canton Bern get only taxed at their residency
